The `sin(log(A+1))` term is highly distinctive - it's a sinusoidal function of a logarithm. Most candidates won't have this.

**Candidates with sin:** 10, 17, 34
**Candidates with log:** 1, 13, 15, 16, 21, 29, 30, 40

The function `sin(log(A+1))` cannot be expressed as:
- Polynomials in A
- `A/(A+c)` (rational functions)
- `exp(c/A)` 
- `A^c` (power functions)
- `log(A+1)` alone
- `exp(A*c)`
- Simple `sin(t)` or `cos(t)`

These are all linearly independent basis functions. `sin(log(A+1))` is a fundamentally different function that oscillates as A grows large, which none of the polynomial, rational, exponential, or simple logarithmic forms can replicate.

Since `sin(log(A+1))` is a unique basis function that appears in none of the candidates (not even in disguised form), **no candidate can match the GT**.
